  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_68f172ca-253a-403a-b16a-6a9d7704655d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48074917?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48074917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16464782948221557082">This was a dumb book. The setting made no sense--they were supposed to be in the 26th century with 18th century technology, but that disjunction was never even hinted at. The characters weren't developed enough to even be caricatures and the book wasn't decent enough to have an ending. Quite literally, the author thought, "hmmm, vampires are cool and pirates are cool and 'vampirates' is witty!" And then he attempted the bare minimum needed to write a book that could be titled Vampirates. And fai</span>
  <span id="freeText16464782948221557082" style="display:none">This was a dumb book. The setting made no sense--they were supposed to be in the 26th century with 18th century technology, but that disjunction was never even hinted at. The characters weren't developed enough to even be caricatures and the book wasn't decent enough to have an ending. Quite literally, the author thought, "hmmm, vampires are cool and pirates are cool and 'vampirates' is witty!" And then he attempted the bare minimum needed to write a book that could be titled Vampirates. And failed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16464782948221557082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161952642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16793994789514986960">Let it be stated for the record that this was purchased for me as a joke. I expected it to be bad. I went into it knowing it was going to be bad. What I didn't know was that it was so much worse than bad, I could never have adequately prepared myself.<br/><br/>First off, it's set in the future. This way, we can talk all about modern things, while still entertaining the thought that pirates still sail the seas in oldie-timey ships, fighting with cutlasses and other oldie-timey things while not having to do</span>
  <span id="freeText16793994789514986960" style="display:none">Let it be stated for the record that this was purchased for me as a joke. I expected it to be bad. I went into it knowing it was going to be bad. What I didn't know was that it was so much worse than bad, I could never have adequately prepared myself.<br /><br />First off, it's set in the future. This way, we can talk all about modern things, while still entertaining the thought that pirates still sail the seas in oldie-timey ships, fighting with cutlasses and other oldie-timey things while not having to do any historical research because, did you forget? We're set in the future, so it doesn't have to be accurate! <br /><br />Then we'll make up a badly rhyming song about Vampire-Pirates to use as a lullaby! Although clearly we will find out later that they aren't as bad as they seem, because like most vampires these days, they are just misunderstood!<br /><br />Just when you think it can't get any worse and you're actually reaching the climax of the book, around 10 pages from the end, the final battle is averted by a corrected mistaken identity, and it turns into a hug fest. I am not even kidding. Then it ends. That's it. <br /><br />This had so much potential. I almost want to see someone competent write a book about Vampirates, because I think it could be really interesting. This book, however, is not. I gave it one star because I didn't see any spelling errors, so I guess there's at least one thing to be said for it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16793994789514986960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1678197316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1678197316" />
    <a title="Asghar Abbas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37421322-asghar-abbas"><img alt="Asghar Abbas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444319622p2/37421322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1678197316?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asghar Abbas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asghar Abbas" href="/user/show/37421322-asghar-abbas">Asghar Abbas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0689872631" href="/book/show/723802.Demons_of_the_Ocean">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1678197316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2272654219425442224"><br/>The premise alone is worth the price of admission. I mean, come on look at the title! How can I not read this ? Or. So I thought, so I thought. And. So he spoke, and so he spoke, that lord of Castamere. Sigh. Why won't life just be a very long composition by the ever sublime Sigur Rós? <br/><br/>This book though is not as deep as this song I am listening to, is making it out to be. But at its core, it is about a pair of twin siblings. I can't seem to escape my fascination with this concept. For, what is m</span>
  <span id="freeText2272654219425442224" style="display:none"><br />The premise alone is worth the price of admission. I mean, come on look at the title! How can I not read this ? Or. So I thought, so I thought. And. So he spoke, and so he spoke, that lord of Castamere. Sigh. Why won't life just be a very long composition by the ever sublime Sigur Rós? <br /><br />This book though is not as deep as this song I am listening to, is making it out to be. But at its core, it is about a pair of twin siblings. I can't seem to escape my fascination with this concept. For, what is more tragic than an idea of twins? Is it not a tragedy to have another you that is just as fallible as you? Your reflection. Only better while you feel like a cracked mirror? <br /><br />At the beginning, this story made me nostalgic for Song of the Sea. Probably because it shared similar themes; a melancholic lighthouse attendant taking care of his motherless children. And mostly because I saw that movie back in the June of last year. One of the reasons why I read this book around this June. <br /><br />I've missed the Song of the Sea. Of course, in the Cartoon Saloon's animated feature, the not children of the forest's mother was a selkie ( can't help imagining Colin Farrell's character saying, What's a selkie in his Irish Brogue in the excellent movie Ondine ) and here, it is hinted the twins' mother might have been a Vampirate. That's a combination of a vampire and a pirate. Or rather a vampire who is also a pirate. You can laugh now. The thing is, the concept was unique but the execution very poor indeed. <br /><br />Anyhow, that was the vibe I was getting before the book delved into the smorgasbord mess of things it just possibly couldn't be. It tried though. But the pacing was really terrible, the characters were all cardboard, cookie-cutter, one-dimensional nonpeople types. With the possible exception of the lovelorn Irish vampy. And like all the fellow victims, others who have suffered this book had pointed out, the vampires and the pirates were a little too friendly and not fiendish enough. <br /><br />There was a LOT of telling, not enough showing in this one, lemme tell you. Look, I get it. <br />This is geared toward kids, it wasn't even a young adult novel, just a children's book, I understand that. <br /><br />But honestly tell me, whatever happened to the charming children's books that educated the young as well the adults? The ones that enthralled the wee ones and helped grow up the grown-ups? The awesomeness likes of Stuart Little, The Iron Giant, Bridge to Terabithia (one of my favorite, favorite things in this Circle of the World), Secret Garden, The Spiderwick Chronicles, and Alice in freaking Wonderland. Whatever happened to those kinds of Books that were just, um, books?<br /><br />I was reading this, vampires on a boat even though they didn't act like vampires, couldn't help but think of Fevre Dream, which all of my friends here on gr seem to be reading right now, haha. Then I came across a character named Nathaniel and of course that reminded me of Only Human, another fine novel. <br /><br />I did however like the little skull logo at the head of each chapter, and all the skulls and crossbones did assuage my sudden bout of homesickness. <br /><br />For one of the main reasons I picked this up in the first place was, I got it in '13. And partly because gleefully stuck in this sweet sticky stasis, it reminded me of my not old but erstwhile room. <br /><br />Oh, how I love what's to come. I do. <br /><br />Do you?</span>
  <a data-text-id="2272654219425442224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_381842681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381842681" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11473232-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545983518p2/11473232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381842681?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/11473232-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381842681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12275710471516035064">I remember reading this book when I was about 10 years old. I know what you're thinking, 10 years old, yeah must be a great book *sarcasm* But honestly, I read the first four books in the series and then I was like wow these were AMAZING! I wish Justin Somper would've written more. And then four years later, I was fooling around on the internet looking up books and googling authors and I stumbled upon Justin's site. He had written 2 more books! I immediatly picked up the fifth book and I have be</span>
  <span id="freeText12275710471516035064" style="display:none">I remember reading this book when I was about 10 years old. I know what you're thinking, 10 years old, yeah must be a great book *sarcasm* But honestly, I read the first four books in the series and then I was like wow these were AMAZING! I wish Justin Somper would've written more. And then four years later, I was fooling around on the internet looking up books and googling authors and I stumbled upon Justin's site. He had written 2 more books! I immediatly picked up the fifth book and I have been OBSSESSED with it! The characters in this series have such great personalities! The Vampirates; Lorcan, Darcy Flotsam, Sidiorio, have such vivid descriptions and are each likeable in their own way. The book starts off with Conner and Grace, who are brother and siter, living in a lighthouse with their father. When he dies, the two decide to take their dad's boat instead of going into foster care or being adopted and journey out into the high seas alone. When their boat gets destroyed in a violent storm, the two siblings are seperated and each partake in two very different destinies. One with pirates and one with Vampirates! Little do they know that there are many secrets to be revealed! And they have a past with the Vampirates that the two never could've expected! There are lots of sword fights, blood and battle as well as chilling scenes where Vampirates become blood thirsty savages. I still can't believe that this book is considered a children's book. I absolutely LOVE this series and I'm going to be 15 soon. It's one of those thrilling fantasy like books that you just can't put down! It's not like one of those dumb unoriginal vampire romances or anything like that, it's an adventurous fast-paced novel with lots of surprises and interesting twists. If you're looking to get away from your boring life then I would definitely suggest curling up with this book and letting Conner and Grace take you away to a world of pirates and vampires!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12275710471516035064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5736679-summer?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5736679-summer?shelf=youth">youth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer873615514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12012524362796564149">There are no words to describe how disappointed I am in this book. I figured I would be a sucker for it instantly since I have a mild obsession with pirates... alas, it is likely this obsession that makes me as disappointed as I am. This is such a great concept- merging pirates and vampires, but it is so poorly executed that this concept alone is the only redeeming factor of the book itself.<br/><br/>GR does a good job giving you a summary, so let me just get right down to the nitty gritty.<br/><br/>1) Where the he</span>
  <span id="freeText12012524362796564149" style="display:none">There are no words to describe how disappointed I am in this book. I figured I would be a sucker for it instantly since I have a mild obsession with pirates... alas, it is likely this obsession that makes me as disappointed as I am. This is such a great concept- merging pirates and vampires, but it is so poorly executed that this concept alone is the only redeeming factor of the book itself.<br /><br />GR does a good job giving you a summary, so let me just get right down to the nitty gritty.<br /><br />1) Where the hell is the plot?<br />- The plot of the book itself is none existant. "Two orphans get thrown overboard by a storm; one gets picked up by regular pirates and one gets picked up by vampirates..." -and that's the beginning of the joke. Literally, NOTHING OF IMPORTANCE happens in the book. <br /><br />2) What the fuck kind of timeline is this?<br />- The vampire Lorcen mentions he was born in 1803 and Grace immediately says "So you're seven hundred and nine years old?" ... that means the year is 2512? Or is that when Lorcen turned into a vampire? Is it the current year? Nobody gives up any clarification on that. Also, Miss Flotsam, the talking figurehead of the vampirate ship, was aboard the Titanic once upon a time? Did the whole world just get trapped in the 1920s for 700 years?<br /><br />3) What the fuck is a Pirate Academy?<br />- You heard me, there is an official government-sanctioned place that exists in this book where people train to become pirates and graduate and have ceremonies at. Last time I checked, pirates were criminals and pirates learn from the school of hard knocks.<br /><br />4) Everybody flies the Jolly Roger<br />- Granted, that was a rather large crew back in the day, but seriously... seriously?!<br /><br />5) Vampirates are boring as shit...<br />- They literally do NOTHING other than drag Grace aboard their ship and have dinner and warn her not to open the curtains during the daytime. <br /><br />... the whole book is just a big slap in the face to everything that is pirates. <br /><br />Excuse me while I go cry now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12012524362796564149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2542761664777616354">The book had a great concept but only meh execution. Why are the pirates and vampires all so nice to each other? Neither of them want to hurt people?! I get that this book is aimed at younger audiences but there isn't even much fighting. And why is it based in the future when it could just as easily be based in the past; there is no inclusion of the idea that it's based in the future when the ice caps have melted and a new age of piracy has emerged except for in the blurb. And this is really unf</span>
  <span id="freeText2542761664777616354" style="display:none">The book had a great concept but only meh execution. Why are the pirates and vampires all so nice to each other? Neither of them want to hurt people?! I get that this book is aimed at younger audiences but there isn't even much fighting. And why is it based in the future when it could just as easily be based in the past; there is no inclusion of the idea that it's based in the future when the ice caps have melted and a new age of piracy has emerged except for in the blurb. And this is really unfortunate because that concept is so rad. The characterisation is not bad, and I like the main characters Conner and Grace. And even the secondary characters have good personalities but it's like the entire concept was watered down. It could have been something great but it honestly missed the mark. I still might foray into the second book just to see how the series progresses.</span>

<div id="review_121501591" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121501591" />
    <a title="Qt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/447538-qt"><img alt="Qt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1196007438p2/447538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121501591?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Qt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Qt" href="/user/show/447538-qt">Qt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/447538-qt?shelf=horror-supernatural">horror-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/447538-qt?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/447538-qt?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/447538-qt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121501591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2788612461310915405">I thought this was quite a fun, easy read! I loved the cast of colorful characters and the intriguing concept, and I really liked how so many of the characters were friendly and nice to our heroes. I will definitely be reading more of this series.<br/><br/>There were a few minor things I wasn't crazy about. I would have liked to learn more about Grace and Connor's world, to get a better idea of what it was like, what "technology" was available, etc. And, maybe it was just me, but it seemed odd how quickly</span>
  <span id="freeText2788612461310915405" style="display:none">I thought this was quite a fun, easy read! I loved the cast of colorful characters and the intriguing concept, and I really liked how so many of the characters were friendly and nice to our heroes. I will definitely be reading more of this series.<br /><br />There were a few minor things I wasn't crazy about. I would have liked to learn more about Grace and Connor's world, to get a better idea of what it was like, what "technology" was available, etc. And, maybe it was just me, but it seemed odd how quickly Connor, the hero, accepted the pirates' actions (that is, looting, stealing, and attacking people).<br />I had thought that he would have some qualms with what they were doing, and I guess he did--but that was only mentioned once, pretty late in the book. I mean, I expect looting and such from pirates and pirate stories ;-) and I really liked the pirates, but I just expected the morality of their actions to be addressed differently. <br />At the end, one plot thread is wrapped up, but others aren't. There are elements of mystery in the book, and I sometimes shared the frustration of Grace, the heroine, who kept getting riddle-like answers in response to her questions. I was hoping that everything--or at least, a lot--would be revealed by the end, but it seemed more like a lot of the answers and action are being saved for the sequel, and this first book just sets you up for it. (Which, of course, is not necessarily a bad thing!)<br /><br />But those are all pretty minor problems, and of course, they aren't all going to bother everyone! I really enjoyed it, and am looking forward to more fun with the characters. The settings and costumes are nicely described and make for some vivid imagery, and I like how, in spite of the vampire and pirate themes, it isn't a gory book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2788612461310915405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelli" href="/user/show/1807931-kelli">Kelli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1807931-kelli?shelf=j-drama-adventure">j-drama-adventure</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41856299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12428320909653474000">I picked this book up to read for the afterschool Book club. I needed a book about pirates and found this one on the shelves. Like Hunger Games, the cover was really holding me up, but I went onward and really liked it. The book is about a set of misfit twins that never seemed to fit in in their small town. Thier father is the Lighthouse keeper and dies suddenly, leaving the twins, Grace and Connor orphaned. The two take their father's boat out to escape foreclosure and the orphange, to sail dow</span>
  <span id="freeText12428320909653474000" style="display:none">I picked this book up to read for the afterschool Book club. I needed a book about pirates and found this one on the shelves. Like Hunger Games, the cover was really holding me up, but I went onward and really liked it. The book is about a set of misfit twins that never seemed to fit in in their small town. Thier father is the Lighthouse keeper and dies suddenly, leaving the twins, Grace and Connor orphaned. The two take their father's boat out to escape foreclosure and the orphange, to sail down to the coast. But a storm brews up and the ship sinks seperating the twins. Grace is rescued by a mysterious ship which she discovers is the Vampirate ship her father sung about to her and her brother when they were scared. Connor is rescued by a Pirate ship and somehow he believes his sister is alive and on the Vampirate ship from the old sea shanty he knows. The book continues of the twins adventures and experiences on the different boats and end with a reunion and opening for the next book. Very quick and intense read! Loved it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12428320909653474000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17463217575080006633">This was a fun little book!<br/><br/>I don't really like vampires, but I love pirates! So it made up for it, and the mix was actually really interesting. The setting is pretty crazy, and the characters are captivating! (I specially liked Molucco Wrathe, such a weird and funny guy! I like weird characters lol)<br/><br/>It may seem like a silly book, as some people pointed out, but that's okay for me.   <span id="freeText17463217575080006633" style="display:none">This was a fun little book!<br /><br />I don't really like vampires, but I love pirates! So it made up for it, and the mix was actually really interesting. The setting is pretty crazy, and the characters are captivating! (I specially liked Molucco Wrathe, such a weird and funny guy! I like weird characters lol)<br /><br />It may seem like a silly book, as some people pointed out, but that's okay for me. After all, it seems to be directed to kids, and I love books for kids...so I enjoy it as it is supposed to be enjoyed, silly and kinda nonsensical! (I hope this makes sense!)<br /><br />The only complaint I have is that the end was kinda rushed, but since this part of a series, I'll forgive it for that. I look forward to reading the next books!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2637569365978103481">I have read this book when I was still a teenager and quite liked it. Now I had a possibility to read the next books in the series, so I decided to read this one again since I didn't remember a lot from the previous time.<br/><br/>Usually, I don't like young adult stories, they are too immature for me. However, this one is not bad. Not as silly as I was afraid it would be. Reading this now, as an adult, is not a bad experience.<br/><br/>Though I decided not to read the next books in this series. I liked this story </span>
  <span id="freeText2637569365978103481" style="display:none">I have read this book when I was still a teenager and quite liked it. Now I had a possibility to read the next books in the series, so I decided to read this one again since I didn't remember a lot from the previous time.<br /><br />Usually, I don't like young adult stories, they are too immature for me. However, this one is not bad. Not as silly as I was afraid it would be. Reading this now, as an adult, is not a bad experience.<br /><br />Though I decided not to read the next books in this series. I liked this story but I'm not that interested in the next ones. If I was younger I would probably do it. But now it's too late. Still, I'm glad it wasn't a total disappointment.</span>

<div id="review_389339168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/389339168" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/389339168?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781417782871" href="/book/show/2403225.Demons_of_the_Ocean">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=library-read">library-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer389339168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7522035947501380134">3.5<br/><br/>When I first saw the name of this series I thought, "Really? Are you serious? I can just imagine what the author was thinking: 'Hey, do you know what's really popular right now? Vampires. And do you know what else is popular? Pirates. I bet I could smash them together and make a mint!"<br/><br/>Ugh. Pass.<br/><br/>But... <br/><br/>I had heard things about it in the one YA group I'm in, which helped to chip away, a bit, at my initial skepticism, and then, recently, I was at the library and they didn't have the book I was l</span>
  <span id="freeText7522035947501380134" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />When I first saw the name of this series I thought, "Really? Are you serious? I can just imagine what the author was thinking: 'Hey, do you know what's really popular right now? Vampires. And do you know what else is popular? Pirates. I bet I could smash them together and make a mint!"<br /><br />Ugh. Pass.<br /><br />But... <br /><br />I had heard things about it in the one YA group I'm in, which helped to chip away, a bit, at my initial skepticism, and then, recently, I was at the library and they didn't have the book I was looking for, and this sort of jumped out and grabbed my attention and I figured, "Why not - what's to lose?"<br /><br />And so I gave it a go and, as my rating suggests, I'm glad that I did.<br /><br />Not that it's not without its flaws. It has some of the same issues many books of its ilk have - what with prodigy like, but outcast children, at the helm, who are just too precocious for their own good and, of course, they have to be made orphans at some point.<br /><br />(Actually, towards the very beginning, I would say it had tones of Lemony Snicket - minus the defining words thing - and I don't say this as a bad thing, 'cause I liked the Series Which Shall Not Be Named (until The End, that is, though it did get bloated in the middle) - but then it started developing its own tone, which was better.)<br /><br />But, anyway, overall I liked it. It was a fun adventure story with love and loss and pirating and even a little bit of scariness. (Though, for those worried about such things, it is just a little bit.)<br /><br />It did annoy me, a bit, that Grace, who is described as being very bright and smart, was so slow on the uptake about what was going on, and that Connor is one of those people who seems to be "a natural" at any and all physical pursuits... but I was mostly able to look over that for the interesting secondary characters and the slight ambiguity of the world itself. <br /><br />(I was confused as to the time period. I'd initially assumed it was set in the past because, ya know, pirates (of the romanticized variety), and the clothes on the cover, but then it talks about cars and things and obviously takes place in a more modern era, which was bit baffling... But there was there was a more interesting ambiguity as to the nature of the pirates, and the captain in particular, which was pretty cool.)<br /><br />Anyway - <br /><br />So, yes, while the title is totally silly sounding - and a bit off-putting because of it - the book was a decently written adventure which I'm glad I read. I look forward to picking up the next in the series.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="7522035947501380134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer15832284438816492396">I have been trying to read a lot of books my sons read/have read or will read. So, I grabbed Vampirates off the shelf. This series was a favorite of my 17 year olds when he was younger and my 12 year old is starting to give it the eye (even though it isn't in his genre).<br/>With a series name like Vampirates it has to be the corniest thing out there, right? Wrong! I am hooked and love these books. I want to read the next one in the series, however, I am trying to get an idea of what different books </span>
  <span id="freeText15832284438816492396" style="display:none">I have been trying to read a lot of books my sons read/have read or will read. So, I grabbed Vampirates off the shelf. This series was a favorite of my 17 year olds when he was younger and my 12 year old is starting to give it the eye (even though it isn't in his genre).<br />With a series name like Vampirates it has to be the corniest thing out there, right? Wrong! I am hooked and love these books. I want to read the next one in the series, however, I am trying to get an idea of what different books are like and review them. For someone who gets engrossed in the story I have a feeling this is going to be torture!<br />The book is about a brother and sister (twins) who have always been a little better at what they do than normal, so the town doesn't love them. Dad dies (mom was gone before the story began). The two orphans, in the wisdom of children, figure their best shot is at sea! <br />They take off on a little boat, encounter a storm and each get rescued by a different ship. They don't know if the other is alive. Connor tries to become a pirate, although I am happy to say he does have some ethical issues. Grace is swept aboard a ship of mystery where she is locked in a room for "her protection".<br />And the adventures begin,and the are non-stop adventures and intrigue. It seems like I gave a lot away,but I ended with my brief summary at page 71, there are 330 pages.<br />I would recommend this for a boy or girl who has been a reluctant reader. The book ends in a place where you have to read the next one, you could even read aloud the first book (or even part of it) and the child will want to keep going!<br />As far as characterization, it isn't complex, but the characters are well thought out. The writing style is easy to follow, but does not use cliches. The writer helps young minds learn by using more difficult words periodically (grotesque for example).</span>
  <a data-text-id="15832284438816492396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="(Ellie) ReadtoRamble" class="user" itemprop="url" name="(Ellie) ReadtoRamble" href="/user/show/24057506-ellie-readtoramble">(Ellie) ReadtoRamble</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3233728491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3853165110302441617">This was one of my picks for the O.W.L.s Magical Readathon that I'm participating in this year. I read it for the prompt of Defence Against the Dark Arts to read a book set at sea/the coast, and I have to say that this book fits the prompt perfectly! <br/>I hadn't heard of this book until a friend recommended it to me, but now I'm so very excited to read the rest of the series. <br/>We follow the story of twins Grace and Connor as they are swept out into the ocean on their father's ship, are separated and</span>
  <span id="freeText3853165110302441617" style="display:none">This was one of my picks for the O.W.L.s Magical Readathon that I'm participating in this year. I read it for the prompt of Defence Against the Dark Arts to read a book set at sea/the coast, and I have to say that this book fits the prompt perfectly! <br />I hadn't heard of this book until a friend recommended it to me, but now I'm so very excited to read the rest of the series. <br />We follow the story of twins Grace and Connor as they are swept out into the ocean on their father's ship, are separated and each end up on a different pirate ship, except, one of the siblings doesn't end up on a normal pirate ship, but the Vampirates ship.<br /><br />I read this book really fast, it had a lot of Lemony Snicket vibes so I found it really witty and sarcastic at times, almost like the twins were doomed from the start, much the same as the Baudelaire children. This story is really jam-packed full of fun, adventures, mystery and I loved every single minute of it. I really liked having the story from both the twins' point of view on their different ships and it gave me a really distinct impression of both pirate lives. I got so many Peter Pan, Lemony Snicket and Pirates of the Caribbean vibes and I had such a fun time reading this first installment in the Vampirates series. I would highly recommend and I look forward to continuing the series! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3853165110302441617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_71847716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71847716" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/725500-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71847716?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/725500-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71847716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15385712211678020034">"If Pirates are bad, and vampires are worse, then I pray that as long as I be, that though I sing of Vampirates, I never one shall see."<br/><br/>That's a verse from a sea shanty often sung in Vampirates. The premise is pretty obvious, right? It's pirates, who are also vampires! How cool is that! Sadly, my own review might read something like:<br/><br/>"If stories of pirates are good, and stories of vampires are better, then though I read the Vampirates, I pray you never do."<br/><br/>Ok, this book isn't THAT bad. Let's get </span>
  <span id="freeText15385712211678020034" style="display:none">"If Pirates are bad, and vampires are worse, then I pray that as long as I be, that though I sing of Vampirates, I never one shall see."<br /><br />That's a verse from a sea shanty often sung in Vampirates. The premise is pretty obvious, right? It's pirates, who are also vampires! How cool is that! Sadly, my own review might read something like:<br /><br />"If stories of pirates are good, and stories of vampires are better, then though I read the Vampirates, I pray you never do."<br /><br />Ok, this book isn't THAT bad. Let's get something straight though, this is actually a kids book. Still, even as a kids book, it's pretty poor. The motivations for the characters are weak, especially the Vampirates... who seem to be a bunch of really nice people, actually. In fact the non-vampire pirates are down right the most pleasant people in the entire book! Maybe the tag line should be: "If pirates are nice, and vampires are nicer, then nothing better could happen then hooking up with the Vampirates!"<br /><br />I want to say this book was a fun read, but it wasn't really... although I admit that it did kinda suck me in. The best thing I can say about it is that is was quick and easy to read. This may be an ideal book for a kid 8-12 years old, depending on how much they think vampires are cool.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15385712211678020034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Good and notorious pirates abound, but there are is a new mysterious breed of pirates - those who seek blood rather than g</span>
  <span id="freeText16360738779991854181" style="display:none">Interest level: 5th +<br />Reading level: medium<br />Genre: adventure, suspense, horror, vampires, pirates<br /><br />If you're looking for an adventure story with an interesting twist, try this new exciting series. Although it has many features of a typical high sea adventure, this series is actually set in the future (2505) and the kind of piracy that exits is unlike any you may have read about. Good and notorious pirates abound, but there are is a new mysterious breed of pirates - those who seek blood rather than gold. They are called vampirates. <br /><br />Connor and Grace, orphaned twins who try to escape a life in a dreary orphanage or - worse - adoption by a horrible couple, take to the sea on their father's yacht. But when they get caught in a storm and almost drown, they are separated - Connor is picked up by a notorious pirate ship and Grace is rescued by a vampirates' ship. From that moment their lives change forever...<br /><br />"Demons of the Ocean" and the "Tide of Terror" are the first two books in the series, both very fast-paced and hard to put down.<br /><br />Take a look at the [ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/bbc7/bigtoe/books/authors/somper.shtml">http://www.bbc.co.uk/bbc7/bigtoe/book...</a> ]BBCís author page to find out about author Justin Somper.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer107016444" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16030931562642915579">I am awarding this single star to Vampirate Lorcan, the only character I actually liked in this book. If I could award half stars, I might award half a star to Darcy, the living figurehead of the Vampirate ship... The narration is essentially a long, long children's book. Perhaps if it was marketed as such and peppered with lovely illustrations by the cover artist, I would feel less irritated by the amount of time I spent looking forward to reading it, reading it, and sighing loudly in exasperat</span>
  <span id="freeText16030931562642915579" style="display:none">I am awarding this single star to Vampirate Lorcan, the only character I actually liked in this book. If I could award half stars, I might award half a star to Darcy, the living figurehead of the Vampirate ship... The narration is essentially a long, long children's book. Perhaps if it was marketed as such and peppered with lovely illustrations by the cover artist, I would feel less irritated by the amount of time I spent looking forward to reading it, reading it, and sighing loudly in exasperation reading the last quarter of the book. None of the characters act as real people would, the emotions and descriptions are flat, and any conflict that might have been is abruptly cut short and swept off to sea. Or perhaps to the next volume. Which I will not be reading. <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText2540848000545573517" style="display:none">This book is a mess and I love it. Vampirates manages to be one of those books that you’re only able to passively read. You get curious over how much is left because nothing has happened yet, and it turns out you’ve finished the book. <br /><br />Obviously aimed at illiterate 8 year olds, this book is a national treasure. I never did figure out if the pirate academy was literal or not. Either way, this book has no subtlety whatsoever with its ‘tell not show’ mentality. Complete with a built in vampirates chanty that Grace and Connor sing every other chapter, that isn’t even foreshadowing??? Either way everyone should know it by heart. If you don’t, get out. <br /><br />In short, 10/10. best book ever. Must read. <br /><br />Can’t wait to get my hands on the rest of the 6 book series. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

The characters had no depth or personality. They felt more like automatons. The plot was horribly lacking in logical or interesting transitions of events into one another. It just felt so unthought about before it was written and I have to wonder if the author made anything past a first draft. Not for me!</span>

  <span id="freeText7173078528637351652" style="display:none">I went into this with low expectations and I’m glad I did because man, was it stupid. It was set like 500 years in the future but there was nothing remotely futuristic about it? Just old-school pirates on wooden boats doing their thing and stealing booty. And then some of them were vampires. There was this one dude who was like Edward Cullen but Irish and a bit less creepy. I felt like I wasn’t allowed to find him hot though because it was a book for kids?? Vampire pirates is generally a great concept and I would love this if it was an actual good YA novel. <br /><br />To summarise, this book was completely dumb but I had a great time reading it and somehow this is the longest review I’ve ever written. I think I need to read the whole series now. That or self-isolation has driven me utterly mad.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_447012'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/447012.Island_Flame"><img alt="Island Flame (Pirates, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1320448836l/447012._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0zQ0dq3yFDV9O4fcueXjiGK4zUR9jvE9swUgB14Z2JqYbo0VsOhk8iU7GY88Z3XS+OcVvIeA5GveVbFgAEYPfA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y6gRrJSfpJbZaInysm51r0WZtx54XDqqIns+0uzgETso8qjPiYXUUYFoF6E37OP138Zv5oJSL/xPK6+1sr/G3Q==')})
